**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy HTTP Filter Chain Registration and Execution

## Your Task

Trace how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. Find C++ and protobuf files across envoyproxy/envoy and envoyproxy/data-plane-api that implement: the FilterChainFactory interface (in envoy/http/), the FilterChainHelper that constructs chains from config, the FilterManager that executes filter chains at runtime, and the HttpConnectionManager proto that defines the filter_chain configuration schema.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2, sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367, sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6, sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2` (envoyproxy/envoy)
- `sg-evals/data-plane-api--84e84367` (envoyproxy/data-plane-api)
- `sg-evals/go-control-plane--71637ad6` (envoyproxy/go-control-plane)
- `sg-evals/grpc--957dba5e` (grpc/grpc)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive trace of how HTTP filter chains are registered and executed in the Envoy proxy. I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings including:

## Key Findings:

### **Files Located:**
- **Configuration**: `envoy/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/v3/http_connection_manager.proto` - Defines the schema
- **Interfaces**: 
  - `envoy/http/filter_factory.h` - FilterChainFactory interface
  - `envoy/http/filter.h` - FilterChainFactoryCallbacks interface
- **Implementation**:
  - `source/common/http/filter_chain_helper.h/cc` - FilterChainHelper and FilterChainUtility
  - `source/extensions/filters/network/http_connection_manager/config.h/cc` - HttpConnectionManagerConfig
  - `source/common/http/filter_manager.h/cc` - FilterManager and DownstreamFilterManager
  - `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.h/cc` - ConnectionManagerImpl and ActiveStream

### **The Registration and Execution Flow:**

1. **Registration Phase**: HttpConnectionManagerConfig's constructor uses FilterChainHelper to process proto-defined filters, creating FilterFactoryCb callbacks for each filter

2. **Runtime Creation**: When a new HTTP stream arrives:
   - ConnectionManagerImpl::newStream() creates ActiveStream
   - ActiveStream initializes DownstreamFilterManager
   - When headers arrive, ActiveStream::decodeHeaders() calls FilterManager::createFilterChain()

3. **Chain Construction**: 
   - FilterManager calls FilterChainFactory::createFilterChain()
   - Which calls FilterChainUtility::createFilterChainForFactories()
   - Which invokes each FilterFactoryCb callback with FilterChainFactoryCallbacks
   - Filters register themselves via addStreamDecoderFilter/addStreamEncoderFilter

4. **Execution**: Decoder filters execute forward, encoder f

execute in reverse order (typical for request/response asymmetry).\\n\\n### Key Design Points\\n\\n1. **Configuration-driven**: Filter chains are defined entirely in protobuf, supporting both static and dynamic (ECDS) configurations\\n2. **Lazy instantiation**: FilterFactoryCb callbacks delay actual filter creation until the stream reaches the filter chain creation point\\n3. **Dual manager pattern**: Separate FilterChainFactory (registration) and FilterChainManager (execution) interfaces provide clean separation of concerns\\n4. **Bidirectional filtering**: Filters can implement decoder-only, encoder-only, or bidirectional interfaces, with execution order automatically handled\\n5. **Upgrade handling**: Special protocol upgrades (WebSocket, CONNECT) get their own filter chain back\\n2. **Encoding**: `FilterManager::encodeHeaders()` iterates through encoder_filters from back to front\\n\\nThis ensures decoder filters execute in configured order, while encoder filters execute in reverse order (typical for request/response asymmetry).\\n\\n### Key Design Points\\n\\n1. **Configuration-driven**: Filter chains are defined entirely in protobuf, supporting both static and dynamic (ECDS) configurations\\n2. **Lazy instantiation**: FilterFactoryCb callbacks delay actual filter creation until the stream reaches the filter chain creation point\\n3. **Dual manager pattern**: Separate FilterChainFactory (registration) and FilterChainManager (execution) interfaces provide clean separation of concerns\\n4. **Bidirectional filtering**: Filters can implement decoder-only, encoder-only, or bidirectional interfaces, with execution order automatically handled\\n5. **Upgrade handling**: Special protocol upgrades (WebSocket, CONNECT) get their own filter chain if configured, falling back to default chain if not\\n6. **Route-based overrides**: Per-route filter configuration allows routes to enable filters disabled by default or override upgrade
